<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immigration">Immigration</span></h3>
<p>Since the overthrow of the regime of <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">Saddam Hussein</a> in 2003, Iraqi Kurdistan has witnessed massive immigration from the rest of Iraq (particularly from Kurds, Assyrians, Armenians, Mandeans, Shabaks), as well as Kurds from other parts of <a href="/wiki/Kurdistan" title="Kurdistan">Kurdistan</a>. Because of the stability and security, Kurdistan has witnessed non-Kurdish or non-Iraqi immigrants.
</p><p>Widespread economic activity between Iraqi Kurdistan and Turkey has given the opportunity for Kurds from Turkey to seek jobs in Iraqi Kurdistan. A Kurdish newspaper based in the Kurdish capital estimates that around 50,000 Kurds from Turkey are now living in Kurdistan<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Reports about immigrant Kurds from <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> and Turkey have been published as well.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Refugees">Refugees</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Refugees_of_the_Syrian_Civil_War" title="Refugees of the Syrian Civil War">Refugees of the Syrian Civil War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_persons_in_Iraq" title="Internally displaced persons in Iraq">Internally displaced persons in Iraq</a></div>
<p>The Kurdistan Region is hosting 1.2 million displaced Iraqis who have been displaced by the ISIS war, as of early December 2017. There were about 335,000 in the area prior to 2014 with the rest arriving in 2014 as a result of unrest in Syria and attacks by the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">Islamic State</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> In addition the Kurdistan Region hosts around 240,000 Syrian refugees who fled the Syrian Civil War, as of January 2018.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Iraqi culture">Iraqi culture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kurdish_culture" title="Kurdish culture">Kurdish culture</a></div>
<p>Kurdish culture is a group of distinctive cultural traits practiced by Kurdish people. The Kurdish culture is a legacy from the various ancient peoples who shaped modern Kurds and their society, but primarily Iranian. Among their neighbours, the Kurdish culture is closest to Persian culture. For example, they celebrate <a href="/wiki/Newroz" class="mw-redirect" title="Newroz">Newroz</a> as the new year day, which is celebrated on March 21. It is the first day of the month of <i>Xakelêwe</i> in Kurdish calendar and the first day of spring.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Other peoples such as <a href="/wiki/Arab_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab culture">Arabs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_culture" title="Assyrian culture">Assyrians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenian_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian culture">Armenians</a>, Shabaks and Mandeans have their own distinctive cultures.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Iraqi music">Iraqi music</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kurdish_music" title="Kurdish music">Kurdish music</a></div>
<p>Traditionally, there are three types of Kurdish classical performers – <a href="/wiki/Storytelling" title="Storytelling">storytellers</a> (<i>çîrokbêj</i>), <a href="/wiki/Minstrel" title="Minstrel">minstrels</a> (<i>stranbêj</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Bard" title="Bard">bards</a> (<i>dengbêj</i>). There was no specific music related to the Kurdish princely courts, and instead, music performed in night gatherings (<i>şevbihêrk</i>) is considered classical. Several musical forms are found in this genre. Many songs are <a href="/wiki/Epic_poetry" title="Epic poetry">epic</a> in nature, such as the popular <i>lawik</i>s which are heroic ballads recounting the tales of Kurdish heroes of the past like <a href="/wiki/Saladin" title="Saladin">Saladin</a>. <i>Heyran</i>s are love ballads usually expressing the melancholy of separation and unfulfilled love. <i>Lawje</i> is a form of religious music and <i>Payizok</i>s are songs performed specifically in autumn. Love songs, dance music, wedding and other celebratory songs (<i>dîlok/narînk</i>), erotic poetry and <a href="/wiki/Work_song" title="Work song">work songs</a> are also popular.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Franso_Hariri_Stadium.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Franso_Hariri_Stadium.JPG/220px-Franso_Hariri_Stadium.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Franso_Hariri_Stadium.JPG/330px-Franso_Hariri_Stadium.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Franso_Hariri_Stadium.JPG/440px-Franso_Hariri_Stadium.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Franso_Hariri_Stadium.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Franso_Hariri_Stadium" title="Franso Hariri Stadium">Franso Hariri Stadium</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Association_Football" class="mw-redirect" title="Association Football">Football</a> is the most popular sport in Iraqi Kurdistan, overseen by the <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Kurdistan_Football_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="Iraqi Kurdistan Football Association">Iraqi Kurdistan Football Association</a>.
KFA submit an application for membership in FIFA. The Kurdistan Premier League is a Kurdish professional league for men's association football clubs. At the top of the Kurdish football league system, it is the country's primary football competition. Contested by 14 clubs, it operates on a system of promotion and relegation.
October 2012, Kurdistan Kickboxing Association (KKA) was officially announced as the new member of <a href="/wiki/World_Kickboxing_Association" title="World Kickboxing Association">World Kickboxing and Karate Association</a> (WKA).
Also member of World Kickboxing and Karate Union (WKU).
In 2012 Kurdistan won the <a href="/wiki/Viva_World_Cup" title="Viva World Cup">Viva World Cup</a> as the host of the tournament.
</p>

<li id="cite_note-31"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-31">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Ammianus Marcellinus, another fourth-century writer.

In his excursus on the Sasanian Empire, he describes Assyria in such a way that there is no mistaking he is talking about lower Mesopotamia (Amm. Marc. XXIII. 6. 15). For Assyria, he lists three major cities&#160;– Babylon, Ctesiphon and Seleucia (Amm. Marc. xxIII. 6. 23)&#160;– whereas he refers to Adiabene as <i>Assyria priscis temporibus vocitata</i> (Amm. Marc. xxIII. 6. 20).</span>
</li>
